The contract period is one year, with a monthly deposit of 500 yuan, totaling 6,000 yuan. Liu and others will first pay two installments of 1,000 yuan.

Plans to Open a Circular Road Around the City: The Bureau of Construction plans to open a circular road around the city, starting from the endpoint of Fengmen, passing through Loumen and Fengmen, and reaching the North Road Bridge in Qimen. It will then be divided into two lines, one directly to the train station and the other to Lu Mu Town, approximately twenty English miles in length. The estimated cost is over ten thousand yuan. There are over a dozen bridges in the middle, requiring a cost of two hundred thousand yuan. It is proposed to levy a fee from all shops in the county to be collected on behalf of the construction, following the method of conscripting labor for road construction.

Wuxi 87

Anti-Smuggling Team Returns to Wuxi After Suppressing Bandits: A large number of salt smugglers recently arrived in Wan Shan Dang, at the border of Suzhou and Wuxi, and opened fire with the Seventh Anti-Smuggling Brigade stationed in Wuxi, killing and wounding several officers and policemen. The anti-smuggling team bravely pursued and killed one bandit leader. The bandit crowd scattered in all directions. At 8:00 PM the day before yesterday, the anti-smuggling team was patrolling near the South Dragon King Temple in Xiasi, near Lili, when they encountered smugglers. They immediately stepped forward to arrest them. The smugglers opened fire to resist arrest, and the anti-smuggling team also opened fire. They fought in the lake for several tens of minutes. The smugglers were outnumbered and defeated, fleeing towards Zhejiang. One bandit boat and one quick-firing gun were captured. Yesterday, Captain Wu of the anti-smuggling team led his troops and boats back to Wuxi.

Yu Qi Boat Robbed Again: A boat from Yuqi Town in the Sixteenth District (Qingcheng City) of the county set sail from the city back to town at around 8:00 PM last night. Unexpectedly, when it reached the Mopan Dun area of Fengzhuang, it was suddenly met by three or four dragon boats. More than ten bandits jumped out of the boats, carrying weapons such as pistols, knives, clubs, and flashlights, and ordered the boat to stop. The boatmen dared not resist and had to stop the boat. The bandits jumped aboard and ransacked the cabins, thoroughly searching the boat. The male and female passengers on the boat were also searched. After half an hour, they left fully looted. It is estimated that over 900 yuan in cash and a box of tin foil were robbed. Afterwards, the Fengzhuang Chamber of Commerce heard the news and pursued them, but the bandits had already fled far away and could not be caught.

Suzhou-Wuxi Telephone Line Scheduled to Open: The long-distance telephone lines of nine counties in Jiangsu Province, including Jiangning, Zhenjiang, and Wujin, have already been connected. Recently, Director Sun of the Department of Construction, considering the commercial development of Suzhou and Wuxi counties, deemed it necessary to connect long-distance telephone lines and specifically instructed Deng Fupei, Director of the Electrical Management Office, to start planning. It is now known that the office has decided to start construction on the Wujin to Wuxi section within days and it can be completed by the end of October. After the Changzhou-Wuxi connection is completed, work will begin on the Wuxi to Suzhou section. This phase of the project is expected to be completed by the end of November.

School Thief with Devious Methods Apprehended: Recently, the Wuxi Provincial College of Education and Wuxi Provincial High School cracked a major theft case. The incident is peculiar and interesting. The process of cracking this case is described below. On the 30th of last month, the Wuxi Sheqiao Provincial College of Education opened its term. Within half an hour, the student dormitories lost long gowns, watches, and other items. The teachers' dormitories had chests and baskets broken open, and money, Western suits, and other items were lost, totaling one or two hundred yuan in value. On the 31st, the teachers' dormitories of the school again lost Western suits, leather shoes, money, and other items. The school suffered such losses for two consecutive days, and the administrators felt uneasy. After repeatedly questioning the gatekeepers, they learned that a young man, wearing a wool serge long gown and yellow leather shoes, had been seen daily, looking very much like a student, claiming to be visiting a certain gentleman at the school. Without waiting for a greeting, he went straight to the dormitory. Therefore, the administrators suspected that this young man might have unethical behavior. They notified various schools in Wuxi to pay attention and assigned students who recognized the young man's face to guard at various schools and inquire in the streets, hoping to crack the case. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 2nd of this month, in the student dormitory of the Provincial High School, a Western-suited teenager was discovered rummaging through boxes and stealing items. They immediately captured him and telegraphed the College of Education to send someone to identify him. As a result, this Western-suited teenager was the same person who had previously claimed to be visiting a certain gentleman at the College of Education. He confessed that he committed the multiple thefts at the College of Education alone. The teenager's name is Zhang Yunxuan, 27 years old, from Luoshe, Wuxi. He habitually impersonates people in the education field to visit students or teachers at various schools, thereby stealing valuable items. The reason he knows the names of the students or teachers of various schools is that he either deceives and asks at the gate or memorizes the names marked on the dormitories, so he can sell his skills. He is indeed cunning.

Changzhou 88

Shu Shan Chamber of Commerce Patrol Team Robbed: The Shu Shan Town Chamber of Commerce in Yixing has a patrol team of over ten men with over ten guns. Recently, because a member of the team, Zhang, was undisciplined, he was dismissed. Zhang held a grudge and secretly colluded with dozens of bandits from Taihu Lake, each carrying guns, and went to the town at around 8:00 PM on the 2nd of this month, surrounded the patrol team, robbed over ten guns, and shot and killed Squad Leader Qi and a team cadre. Before leaving, they also kidnapped the head of the Chamber of Commerce, Li, to a boat and sailed towards Taihu Lake, and his fate is still unknown. At that time, the shops and residents in the town were extremely frightened. Fortunately, the bandits did not interfere with other households after searching and robbing the patrol team.

Notorious Bandit Arrested in Luoshuwan: Gong Bolin, a notorious bandit leader from Gongjiatang in Luoshuwan, Third District of Wu County, had repeatedly committed robbery and murder. The authorities had repeatedly ordered his arrest. The bandit fled to Shanghai and had not been caught. Unexpectedly, the bandit secretly returned home on the 1st of this month after Wu Dan launched a large-scale bandit suppression campaign. Wei Zhen, the director of the Ben Niu Public Security Second Bureau, learned of this and led a team to surround Gongjiatang at around 1:00 AM on the 3rd. Director Wei entered the house and saw the bandit Gong lying on the bed. He immediately stepped forward to arrest him and escorted him to the Ben Niu Bureau. After a preliminary trial with the Wu Dan Joint Defense Association, it was decided to send police officers to the county on the 5th for interrogation.

Initiating a Six-County Joint Defense: County Magistrate Wu of Wu County, considering the recent rampant banditry and the particularly severe suffering in areas bordering neighboring counties, specifically initiated a joint defense with six counties, including Danyang, Yixing, Yangzhong, Jiangyin, and Liyang, to organize a large-scale joint defense office. It is proposed to publicly recommend Regiment Commander Wu as the director, and the county magistrates of each county as the deputy directors, to achieve effective command. On the 4th, letters were sent to each county, and after receiving approval, they will be jointly submitted to the higher authorities for approval.

Quota for Customs Bonds Changed to 160,000 Yuan: Wu County was ordered to solicit customs duty treasury bonds, previously set at 100,000 yuan. Now, the Department of Finance has approved the use of two yuan added to the rice tax commutation to be used as collateral for borrowing. Therefore, it has reallocated the quota based on the number of rice taxes to be collected. Wujin must raise 160,000 yuan. County Magistrate Wu received the above order yesterday.

Jiangyin 89

Commissioning of Investigation of Opium Case: Li Shaoming, a platoon leader of the Special Service Company of the Fortress Headquarters and the Police Team, discovered on the 15th of last month near Liuwei Port that the Lianhe Wheel had dropped opium, which was being transported by the Water Police Chen Bingquan and others. All the witnesses were to be tried by a military court, and the Department ordered the county government to severely handle the case. Yesterday, Director Hu of the Department of Civil Affairs commissioned inspectors Lu Yong and Huang Laicheng to investigate and interrogate the Water Police Platoon Leader Chen Bingquan, Water Police Liu Hanbing, boatman Pan Bingsheng, etc. The confessions of each person were evasive. After interrogation, it was discovered that the commander of the Twentieth Brigade, He Dian'ao, was involved in transporting opium. Director Hu dismissed him from his post as punishment and appointed Shen Hualong, the former director of the Fengxian Public Security Bureau (a native of Qingyang, Jiangyin), to fill the position.

Nantong 90

Dispatching Warships to Patrol Along the River Ports: The Provincial Security Department convened county magistrates and local representatives from the eight counties of Tongtai to hold a meeting in Tongcheng to discuss bandit suppression. It was generally agreed that bandits have been secretly transporting weapons in various ports along the river recently and that measures should be taken to investigate and crack down on them. It was resolved to request the province to dispatch police warships to be regulated by Li Changjiang, the temporary commander of the bandit suppression campaign. The provincial government has approved the dispatch of the Bo Xian and Jun He warships to specifically patrol the river ports of each county in Tongshu.

Victory in Bandit Suppression in Yu Dong: The provincial and county police team suppressed bandits in the areas of Ding Jiayuan and Yingchang Temple in Yu Dong. At 8:00 PM on the 3rd, they killed over twenty bandits and seized over ten Mauser pistols.

Education Bureau Releases Foundation Land Along the City Walls: Tongyi City Base is currently expanding and building a circular road around the city. The Education Bureau is releasing the foundation land along the city walls for lease, from the northeast Shuiguan Bridge to the south, up to Bianyimen, at a uniform price of twenty yuan per square.

Headquarters Sends Personnel to Inspect Wounded Soldiers: The General Headquarters sent specialists Xi Yun, Yang Linfu, and Hu Wei to Nantong to inspect wounded soldiers. On the 4th, they went to the Thirty-first Rear Hospital to inspect. On the 4th, they left Nantong for Wuhu. Furthermore, the General Headquarters Command sent Wu Yangbo from Jiangyin to Nantong to investigate wounded soldiers.

Salt Smugglers Disturb Tongshu: Large groups of salt smugglers have recently gathered within the territory of Tongshu, using Daan Port as a den, causing serious disturbances. Private salt is rampant in urban and rural areas.

Gaoyou 91

District Chief Subject to Thorough Investigation: Wu Kai, the former district chief of the eighth district of this county, was previously the head of eighteen townships, including Manyang, and was accused of many bad deeds by the Ministry of Civil Affairs and the county government. The Ministry of Civil Affairs has ordered the county government to thoroughly investigate and report the facts for verification.

Robbery Case in Xiaojingou: A fishing boat was passing through Xiaojingou in the county when it was suddenly attacked by many bandits, each wielding guns, who ordered it to stop. They swarmed onto the boat, ransacked it, and shot the fisherman in the leg. Subsequently, a grain boat passed by and was also ransacked. The losses are said to be significant.

Rampant Salt Smugglers in the Fourth District: A large group of salt smugglers has recently appeared in the Fourth District of the county, carrying over ten boats loaded with smuggled salt. Each carried guns, landed on the shore, and left packages at each house, demanding high prices. Anyone who disobeyed would have their houses set on fire. The farmers could not bear the disturbance. Citizens Zhang Xibin and others in the district have submitted a request to the county government to dispatch a team to arrest them.

Danyang 92

Police Team Captures Bandit Leader: Bandits were discovered in the Longwang Temple area bordering Wu Dan and Yang Counties. County Magistrate Shen specifically dispatched Police Chief Sun Long to lead a team to suppress them. They captured Tao Yuanlong, a notorious bandit leader, in the Heimqiao area and escorted him to the county yesterday for imprisonment.

Bandits Kill Villagers: Multiple bandits suddenly broke into Xiecun in Xixiang last night, firing guns to show their strength, intending to rob. Two villagers from the village were walking when they heard the alarm and ran to escape. One was shot and killed by the bandits, and the other was seriously injured. Fortunately, farmers from the neighboring village came to their rescue, and the bandits fled far away.

Yangzhou 93

Meeting to Raise Customs Bonds: The Jiangdu County Government, having received an order from the provincial government, forwarded by the Commander-in-Chief, that the county should be allocated 80,000 yuan of customs bonds, specifically convened the Chamber of Commerce, salt industry tycoons, and gentry at 10:00 AM today (the 4th) at the county government to discuss the allocation method. It was resolved that the Chamber of Commerce would contribute 25,000 yuan, the salt industry 15,000 yuan, the gentry 8,000 yuan, and the remaining 32,000 yuan would be allocated to the various districts in the four townships.

Response to the Dispute Over Boundary Lines: The case of the dispute over the southern boundary of the Xu Fu Guan Town in Henan between the First District and the Second District of the county was instructed by the county government to be investigated and reported by the Public Security Bureau. It is now heard that the county government has received the bureau's report, which states that since the southern part of the town belongs to the boundary of the Second District, all the house numbers of the First District compiled by the former Fifth Sub-bureau should be revoked to clarify the boundaries. As for the public security police station set up at the bus station, it was established by the station with the approval of the Public Security Bureau, specifically to protect the station and is different from ordinary police stations. Whether to change its name, be directly managed by the bureau, or be assigned to the Second Sub-bureau for management should be reviewed and decided by the bureau.

Zhenjiang 94

Various Associations Oppose Telephone Price Increase: The Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce previously telegraphed the Ministry of Communications to temporarily suspend the telephone price increase due to opposition from users. The Ministry of Communications replied to the association that it was difficult to approve. Now, various trade associations in the city plan to strive unanimously and will not stop until they achieve their goal. It is heard that the Chamber of Commerce is also continuing to petition the ministry.

Petition from Disaster Victims of Land Subsidence in Xinzhou: The area near Wanjiang in Xinzhou, Jiangdu County, suddenly collapsed last night, approximately seven or eight mu in circumference. Yesterday, over a hundred disaster victims from the area came to the province to petition the Ministry of Civil Affairs, requesting a place to settle down. It is heard that the Ministry of Civil Affairs has agreed to find a way to resettle them.

Jingjiang 95

Compilation of Kidnapping Cases: At around 5:00 PM the day before yesterday, over twenty bandits, each wielding short and long guns, suddenly entered the Lishiqiao Town in the Eighth District, ordering all shops to close. Many other bandits prohibited the defense corps from going out. Then, they kidnapped Yang Guisan, who had served as a police officer, and killed Gong Chunfa at Yangjiaqiao. On the 30th, a man named Qu, whose mother was seriously ill, led his wife from Wujin back to his hometown. While passing through Zhaojiaweitou in Lishiqiao, four or five bandits suddenly emerged from the fields and robbed Qu's luggage and silver dollars, losing approximately seventy yuan. In Guan Yin Tang, northwest of the Tushao in the Second District, Geng Zhengji, who worked as a farmer, had a small fortune. Suddenly, several bandits kidnapped him the night before last, demanding 500 yuan. That same night, the Li family received a threatening letter, stating that they must raise 1,000 yuan within five days, or there would be consequences. Also, seven or eight bandits went to the home of Zhang Suobao in Yun Chuan Dai, about three li south of Jiajishi in the Third District, ransacked the house, and, finding nothing, kidnapped Suobao, his thirteen-year-old grandson, and his eighteen-year-old niece and went northwest.

Large Quantity of Guns and Ammunition Seized in Xin Gang: The day before yesterday, a small boat was moored in Xin Gang. It departed in the morning and returned to the port slowly in the evening, its movements suspicious. An agency in the port ordered it to dock and inspected it, finding a dozen Mauser pistols and some ammunition. The boatman was detained and interrogated strictly and was taken into custody.

Bandit Leader Li Zhenguo Surrenders: Taihing bandit leader Li Zhenguo (aka Li Jigen) had over a thousand followers, rampaging through Rutaijing. Although the government troops had launched painful suppression campaigns, they were never wiped out. This time, due to internal strife and fearing for his life, he led his subordinates to Major Yang of the Provincial Police Corps in Huangqiao to surrender and turned over over seven hundred long and short guns.

Chen Qinglang Apprehended: Chen Qinglang, who lived in Xieqiao in the Second District, joined the Communist Party in the winter of the 17th year of the Republic through an introduction. At that time, Mao Xueqin, a Jiangyin bandit leader, was in Xieqiao and saw that he was capable, so he ordered Huo Shufang Maosong to give him a Mauser pistol and thirty rounds of ammunition. Mao was executed in Cheng, and Chen sold the weapons and ammunition to Yuan Zumou for 50 yuan. After Fang Maosong came to Jingjiang to surrender this time, he told the county party headquarters about this matter. Last night, he rushed to Xieqiao and arrested Chen Qinglang and escorted him to the city.

Changshu 96

Dispute Over Telephone Price Increase: The Electricity and Telephone Users Association has sent a letter to the company informing it of its intention to remove the equipment if the price increases and stating that users will not be responsible for monthly fees starting August 10. All of this has been reported to the county government and the county party headquarters for the record. At the same time, the progress has been reported to the higher authorities. However, the company's attitude towards collecting the original price remains firm and has telegraphed the provincial department, accusing the Users Association of instigating and so on. The county party headquarters mediated and summoned representatives from both the company and the users to the headquarters for talks. The chairman of the company said that the price would be increased after three months. The association held an emergency meeting on the 3rd, attended by executive committee members and eighteen representatives. It was resolved that, in order to respect the mediation intention of the party headquarters, the users could agree to the company increasing the price by half from the 20th year of the Republic (i.e., 2.5 jiao for those paying half a yuan and 5 jiao for those paying one yuan) for a period of three years, with no further increases within the limit, and a contract must be signed for both parties to abide by. The resolved intention was immediately reported to the party headquarters by the original representatives Li Baojun, Shao Yufan, etc.

Jiaxing 97

Kidnapping in Yu Xian District: At dusk the day before yesterday, several thugs wearing gray clothes suddenly came to the home of Huang Chuanxiang in the Luejiaobang area of Zhengucun, which borders Wangdian District in Jiaxing Yuxian District. They asked if Huang Chuanxiang was at home. Because Huang was out, his relative Jia came out to see them and said that Huang was not at home. If they had anything to say, they could say it for her to pass along. The thug then took out a pistol from his pocket and shouted loudly. At the same time, six or seven people hiding outside also swarmed in and ran into the bedroom and kidnapped Huang's own seven-year-old child. His whereabouts are still unknown. Meat Industry Representatives Petition the Province: Jiaxing previously decided to increase the slaughter tax by 40% at the county government meeting to be used for education and public welfare expenses. Subsequently, the fresh meat industry requested that the county be ordered to exempt them from the increase due to the difficult situation of the Suzhou merchants. The province ordered the county to investigate the commercial situation and submit a proposal for review. However, the county government's reply stated that the 40% increase was still necessary. Therefore, the industry nominated Qian Yuting, Chen Baoshan, and two others to go to the province to petition again. It is now heard that after receiving the petition, the provincial government stated that the case had already been ordered to be based on the financial education of the two departments of the case, and that the county should investigate the industry's situation again, make proper suggestions, and submit them for further review. The previous situation was reported to the case, and it should be reviewed again after the department has reviewed and replied. Yesterday, the instructions were issued and notified.

Jiashan 98

Silk and Cotton Boat Robbed: Shen Haoran, a merchant from Nanxun, Huzhou, sells silk and cotton for a living. He took the goods out for sale one day, and yesterday in Jinze Yuan dang, he suddenly encountered bandits and was robbed along with the boat, losing more than 600 yuan. Boatmen Chu Taiguan and Fan Jingquan were forced to row the boat, while Shen was beaten and injured and pushed to the beach. It was inconvenient to carry the boat to Jinze. Today, they arrived at Shan Station and returned home to find a way to rescue them.

Discontinuation of the Wounded Soldier Liaison Office: After the establishment of the Thirty-fourth Rear Hospital in Jiashan, local agencies immediately organized a wounded soldier liaison office. However, due to two conflicts between the wounded soldiers and the security team, a request was made to the province, and a team was dispatched to escort 600 people to the province. The rear hospital here has also been organized, so the wounded soldier liaison office was immediately closed and discontinued. A total of more than 10,000 yuan was advanced.

Huzhou 99

Xu Jinlian Kidnapped in Nango Bridge: Xu Jinlian, a farmer who lives two li away from Nango Bridge, outside the north gate of the city, at Jiushi Mu Wei, is a tenant farmer with a small fortune. At around 11:00 PM on the 2nd of this month, over twenty bandits, speaking in Shandong and Henan accents, suddenly came and broke down the door, ransacking the house and robbing at will. Before leaving, they kidnapped Jinlian. At that time, Shen Tuanzong of the Nango Bridge Defense Corps heard the news and immediately led the corps to pursue them, but there was no trace of the bandits.

Inspection of the Gospel Hospital: Jiao Tuanzhang of the Second Regiment of the Security Team of this city went to the Gospel Hospital in the south gate of this city at around 3:00 PM yesterday to inspect the hospital wards for bandits mixed in among the patients. In the first-class ward of the hospital, a man named Shen Menlu, from Sian, was found with knife wounds on his head, hands, feet, and other parts. The wounds were numerous and his condition was extremely serious. When asked about the cause of the injuries, he hesitated. In the ordinary room, a man named Liu Genyuan, claiming to be a coal miner from Changxing, was found suffering from gonorrhea. When questioned, he looked flustered. Director Jiao thought that the two men were highly suspicious, so after questioning them, he immediately instructed the hospital to pay attention to them and ordered his men to investigate the truth in various places and then deal with them.

Education News

Important News: Resolution of Education and Cultural Expenditure Issue 100

An Increase of Over 3,428,000 Yuan Compared to Last Year

The Ministry of Education previously drafted the national education and cultural expenditure budget for the nineteenth year and consulted the Ministry of Finance for review and compilation. The Ministry of Finance stated that the second-level expenditure budget for education and culture in the nineteenth year included various agencies and undertakings. In addition to the Central Education Museum, which is a new undertaking and had no recurring expenses listed last year, the Finance Committee had reviewed and approved a total of 13,712,055 yuan at various times. The budget for this year lists recurring expenditures totaling 17,140,645 yuan, an increase of 3,428,590 yuan compared to the total amount approved last year. The recurring expenses of the Ministry of Education headquarters also increased by 108,000 yuan. Given the current financial difficulties and the huge expenditure of the national treasury, there is no room for further expansion of military and political expenses in the nineteenth year. It was specifically requested that the Central Political Conference decide whether to appropriately reduce the budget. The Central Political Conference handed it over to the Finance Group for review. According to the reply, the national education and cultural expenditure budget should be handled in accordance with the detailed rules for the nineteenth year's budget relief measures to ensure uniformity. The 240th meeting of the conference resolved to handle it according to the review opinions and has sent a letter to the Executive Yuan to instruct the Ministry of Finance to comply. (Daily News)

Ministry of Education

Regulations for Setting Up Middle Schools 101

Educational News Agency, Beijing Dispatch: The Ministry of Education has stipulated standards for setting up middle schools and ordered all provinces and cities to comply. The standards are as follows: (A) General Senior Middle School: 1. The annual educational expenditure of a province must be over one million yuan; 2. The total number of graduates from all public and registered private junior middle schools and schools of equivalent level in the province must be over 500 per year for the most recent three years; 3. The percentage of graduates from the aforementioned schools who continue their education must be over 20% in the most recent three years. (B) Agricultural or Technical Senior Middle School: 1. The annual educational expenditure of a province must be over one million yuan; 2. The total number of graduates from all public and registered private junior middle schools and schools of equivalent level in the province must be over 400 per year for the most recent three years; 3. The percentage of graduates from the aforementioned schools who continue their education must be over 20% in the most recent three years. (C) Junior Middle School or Vocational School: 1. The educational expenditure of a city or county must be over 30,000 yuan, and sufficient additional funds must be raised without affecting compulsory education and adult education; 2. The total number of graduates from all complete primary schools and schools of equivalent level in the city or county must be over 300 in the most recent three years; 3. The percentage of graduates from the aforementioned schools who continue their education must be over 25% per year in the most recent three years; 4. There must be no public junior middle school or vocational school in nearby neighboring areas.

Results of the Central Government's Examination for Party Doctrine Teachers Announced 102

The Central Government's Examination Committee for Party Doctrine Teachers has completed this year's examination. The results were officially announced yesterday. The names of the qualified teachers are listed below: Chen Anren, Mou Zhenxi, Huang Zudu, Zhou Feicheng, Lin Zhifu, Lei Zhen, Yu Senwen, Wang Zhixin, Lu Wenhua, Li Hongyin, Chen Xiexun, Bao Shoumei, Sun Mujia, Hu Lifeng, Mao Yingzhang, Ma Wei, and sixteen others have been issued certificates by the committee.

Mandarin Phonetic Symbols Training Class Concludes 103

The Mandarin Phonetic Symbols Training Class for personnel from central government and capital city party and government organs, sponsored by the Ministry of Education, will conclude soon. The instructors are currently compiling detailed lists to evaluate the performance of the participants and will issue certificates with grade reports at the closing ceremony so that the various organs can have a basis for assessment. In the future, when the various organs organize training classes, those with excellent grades will be appointed as instructors. The Ministry of Education's letter to the various party and government organs is recorded below:

This Ministry's Mandarin Phonetic Symbols Training Class for personnel from central government and capital city party and government organs was originally scheduled to continue until the end of this month. However, due to the upcoming start of classes at National Central University, it is necessary to reclaim the classrooms for its own use. Therefore, the hours have been increased in advance to shorten the time. It is estimated that by the 5th of this month, all study courses and examination results can be completed. A meeting will be held at 9:00 AM on the 6th of this month in the Science Hall of National Central University to open the conference and issue certificates. A special letter is hereby issued to inform you. Please check and inform the personnel originally sent by your department to attend the meeting on time.

Secondary and Higher Education

Qualification of Graduates Before Closure 104

Ministry of Education Directive to the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education

The Ministry of Education, based on a report from the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education regarding the qualification of graduates from private secondary and higher education schools before their closure, recently instructed the bureau as follows: Your report has been noted. If private secondary and higher education schools were previously approved for establishment and then ordered to close or voluntarily closed due to poor management or other reasons, the qualifications of their graduates before the closure are naturally valid and do not need to be re-evaluated through screening tests or pre-entrance exams. As for graduates from private secondary and higher education schools that were not registered before being ordered to close or voluntarily closed, those who wish to transfer or continue their education should follow the Ministry's Order No. 695 and Public Notice No. 13 and undergo screening tests or pre-entrance exams. You are hereby informed.

Foreign Teachers 105

Free to Take Oath and Study Party Doctrine

The Ministry of Education, based on a request from the National Conservatory of Music, asked whether foreign teachers should take a supplementary oath and join the study of Party doctrine. The Ministry of Education instructed the school that foreign teachers are free to participate in the oath-taking ceremony, and if there are difficulties in group study of Party doctrine, the school can purchase translated versions of materials on the Party's doctrine for them to study freely. You are hereby informed.

This Locality

This City's School Calendar for This Year 106

The Municipal Bureau of Education recently revised the school calendar for the 19th year of the Republic of China for this city, based on the Central Government's concise list of revolutionary anniversaries, and has submitted it to the Municipal Government for approval and record. The school calendar is recorded below:

Revised Shanghai Municipal School Calendar for the 19th Year 107

August 1st, 19th year (Friday): First semester begins.

On the same day, colleges and universities begin handling enrollment matters.

15th (Friday): Primary and secondary schools begin handling enrollment matters.

20th (Tuesday): First semester classes begin for primary schools.

On the same day, Memorial Day for Martyr Liao Zhongkai (no holiday): Hold a memorial ceremony and lecture on Mr. Liao's history of martyrdom, and send representatives to participate in the memorial meeting of the senior Party headquarters.

25th (Monday): First semester classes begin for secondary schools.

27th (Wednesday): Confucius' Birthday (holiday): Hold a memorial ceremony and lecture on Confucius' life.

September 1st (Monday): First semester classes begin for colleges and universities.

9th (Tuesday): Anniversary of the Premier's First Uprising (no holiday): Hold a memorial ceremony, lecture on the social situation at the time and its impact, and send representatives to participate in the memorial meeting of the senior Party headquarters.

21st (Sunday): Memorial Day for Martyr Zhu Zhixin: Hold a memorial ceremony and lecture on Mr. Zhu's history of martyrdom, and send representatives to participate in the memorial meeting of the senior Party headquarters.

October 10th (Friday): National Day (holiday): Hang flags and decorations, gather to celebrate, commemorate the Wuchang Uprising, and lecture on the founding history of the Republic of China.

11th (Saturday): Anniversary of the Premier's Peril in London (no holiday): Hold a memorial ceremony, lecture on the Premier's ordeal in London, and send representatives to participate in the memorial meeting of the senior Party headquarters.

November 12th (Wednesday): Premier's Birthday (holiday): Hang flags to celebrate, gather to commemorate, and lecture on the Premier's revolutionary history.

December 5th (Friday): Anniversary of the Zhaohe Warship Uprising (no holiday): Hold a memorial ceremony, lecture on the history of the Zhaohe Warship Uprising, and send representatives to participate in the memorial meeting of the senior Party headquarters.

21st (Sunday): Winter vacation begins for all levels of schools.

25th (Thursday): Anniversary of the Yunnan Uprising (no holiday): Hold a memorial ceremony, commemorate the Yunnan Uprising, lecture on the history of overthrowing the imperial system, and send representatives to participate in the memorial meeting of the senior Party headquarters.

January 1st, 20th year (Thursday): Anniversary of the Founding of the Republic of China (holiday): Hang flags and decorations, gather to celebrate, commemorate the Nanjing government, and lecture on the Premier's history of nation-building.

10th (Saturday): Winter vacation ends for all levels of schools.

11th (Sunday): Continue classes after the winter vacation.

24th (Saturday): Semester exams begin for secondary schools.

26th (Monday): Semester exams begin for primary schools.

31st (Saturday): First semester ends.

February 1st (Sunday): Second semester begins.

On the same day (Sunday) to the 7th (Saturday), colleges and universities have a semester transition period with no classes, during which they complete school affairs from the previous semester, handle enrollment matters for this semester, implement guidance on employment and further education, and course selection. All students must go to school to engage in beneficial extracurricular activities.

On the same day (Sunday) to the 5th (Thursday), secondary schools have a semester transition period with no classes, following the same procedures as colleges and universities.

On the same day (Sunday) to the 3rd (Tuesday), primary schools have a semester transition period with no classes, following the same procedures as colleges and universities.

4th (Wednesday): Second semester classes begin for primary schools.

6th (Friday): Second semester classes begin for secondary schools.

8th (Sunday): Second semester classes begin for colleges and universities.

March 12th (Thursday): Anniversary of the Premier's Death (holiday): Gather to mourn and lecture on the history of the Kuomintang.

18th (Wednesday): Anniversary of the Beijing People's Revolution (no holiday): Hold a memorial ceremony, lecture on the history of the Beijing People's Revolution, and the darkness of the government at the time, and send representatives to participate in the memorial meeting of the senior Party headquarters.

21st (Saturday): Local Memorial Day: Hold a memorial ceremony (no holiday), commemorate the recapture of Shanghai, and lecture on the process of Shanghai's recapture.

29th (Sunday): Revolutionary Martyrs' Memorial Day: Hold a memorial ceremony, lecture on the deeds of the revolutionary martyrs, and participate in the senior Party headquarters' sacrifice and memorial meeting.

April 4th (Saturday): Spring break begins for all levels of schools.

6th (Monday): Spring break ends for all levels of schools.

12th (Sunday): Purge the Party Memorial Day: Hold a memorial ceremony, lecture on the Chinese Communist Party's harm to the country and the process of purging the Party, and send representatives to participate in the memorial meeting of the senior Party headquarters.

May 5th (Tuesday): Anniversary of the Revolutionary Government (holiday): Hang flags and gather to celebrate, lecture on the significance of the Premier taking office as Grand President.

9th (Saturday): National Humiliation Memorial Day (no holiday): Gather to commemorate and lecture on the causes and consequences of the National Humiliations on May 9th, August 29th, and September 7th, and the significance of abolishing unequal treaties.

18th (Monday): Memorial Day for Martyr Chen Yingshi (no holiday): Hold a memorial ceremony, lecture on Chen Yingshi's revolutionary history, and send representatives to participate in the memorial meeting of the senior Party headquarters.

June 9th (Tuesday): Colleges and universities begin handling matters related to the end of the second semester.

15th (Monday): Secondary schools begin handling matters related to the end of the second semester.

16th (Tuesday): Anniversary of the Premier's Peril in Guangzhou (no holiday): Hold a memorial ceremony, lecture on the Premier's ordeal in Guangzhou, and send representatives to participate in the memorial meeting of the senior Party headquarters.

17th (Tuesday): Primary schools begin handling matters related to the end of the second semester.

23rd (Tuesday): Summer vacation begins for colleges and universities.

29th (Monday): Summer vacation begins for secondary schools.

July 1st (Wednesday): Summer vacation begins for primary schools.

9th (Thursday): Anniversary of the Northern Expedition Oath-Taking Ceremony of the National Revolutionary Army (holiday): Hang flags and gather to celebrate, lecture on the historical mission and the process of the Northern Expedition of the National Revolutionary Army.

31st (Friday): Second semester ends.

Explanation 108

1. This calendar stipulates that summer vacation for colleges and universities is limited to 70 days, for secondary schools 56 days, and for primary schools 50 days. Winter vacation for all levels of schools is limited to 21 days, and spring break for all levels of schools is set at three days. Memorial holidays total eight days, in accordance with the Regulations on School Year, Semester, and Holiday Dates promulgated by the Ministry of Education.

2. Each school may take one day off for its founding anniversary, but for anniversaries that are multiples of five or ten years, two days off may be taken.

3. Each school should independently determine the types of gatherings for memorial weeks and all detailed items related to school conduct and incorporate them into the school calendar and report it to this bureau for record.

Local News

Yesterday's General Meeting of the Chinese Ratepayers' Association 125

▲ Resignation of Chinese Director Bei Songsun

▲ Hu Mengjia Elected as Successor

▲ Opposition to Water Rate Increase

The Shanghai Public Concession Chinese Ratepayers' Association held a general meeting of representatives yesterday afternoon at 3:30 PM at the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce. Presided over by Wang Xiaolai, the meeting lasted two hours. Regarding the matter of Chinese Director Bei Songsun of the Municipal Council requesting to resign due to his upcoming trip abroad to study banking for six months, it was resolved to approve the request. Hu Mengjia was immediately elected to succeed him. Subsequently, the discussion focused on opposing the proposed 25% increase in water rates. The atmosphere in the meeting became tense, with numerous speakers expressing their views. Ultimately, three opposition measures were decided upon and will be actively pursued until the goal is achieved. Details are as follows:

▲ Meeting Circumstances

The meeting was originally scheduled to begin at 2:00 PM yesterday, but due to the late arrival of representatives, it was delayed until 3:30 PM. Chairman Wang Xiaolai then announced the commencement of the meeting. The representatives present were Zhang Rulin, Zou Quan, Hu Xisheng, Zou Xieqing, Fang Jiaobo (represented by Wu Yayin), Wu Yayin, Li Bohan, Sun Qiuping, Chen Tianyin, Qin Runqing, Yuan Jinchu, Yu Xiji, Xie Zhongfu, Zhang Zilian, Pan Xulun, Wang Jiean, Zhang Yichen, Lu Feibohong, Zhu Peiyuan, Hu Fengxiang, Cheng Xiechun, Lin Kanghou, Chen Tingrui (representing Lin Kanghou), Yu Zhongxian, Yan Esheng, Chen Gengxin, Jiang Yinan, Xu Yunan, Chu Huiseng, Lu Fengzhu, He Shaogeng, Yuan Ludeng, Zhao Jinqing, Hu Mengjia (represented by Xu Jiliao), Li Fusun, Wu Yunzhai, Wang Xiaolai, Sun Jingxi, Zhang Henghai, Wang Yansong, Lu Wenshao, Zhang Yichen, and Shen Tianxin. In attendance were Chinese Councilors Yu Qiaqing, Liu Hongsheng, Xu Jiliao, Qian Longzhang, representatives from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Liu Yunfang, and representatives from the Shanghai Municipal Government Geng Jiaji. The agenda was as follows: 1. Opening of the meeting; 2. Three bows to the national flag, party flag, and Dr. Sun Yat-sen's portrait; 3. Recitation of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's will; 4. Chairman's report on the purpose of the meeting; 5. Discussion of Director Bei Songsun's resignation from the Municipal Council; 6. Discussion of opposition to the Shanghai Waterworks Company's proposed 25% rate increase.

▲ Re-election of Chinese Director

The chairman first reported that recent discussions by the Standing Committee and Executive Committee were deemed to have no power to decide, hence the submission to today's general meeting for discussion. Yu Qiaqing then stated that Director Bei Songsun possessed extraordinary courage and quick thinking, making him an invaluable talent. If his departure from Shanghai were short-term, they would certainly make every effort to retain him. However, since his absence would last for more than six months, the voting rights of the Chinese at the Municipal Council meetings were indispensable. Losing one of them would undoubtedly have a negative impact. Therefore, for the benefit of the majority of citizens, they had no choice but to accommodate the situation and re-elect a replacement. A majority agreed, and the chairman put it to a vote, which passed unanimously. Hu Fengxiang proposed changing the agenda to immediately hold a re-election, which Chu Huiseng seconded and was unanimously approved. Qian Longzhang and Pan Xulun were appointed as vote counters. As a result, Hu Mengjia was elected as a director of the Municipal Council with 29 votes (Chen Guangfu received the second highest number of votes with seven votes). The election was signed and sealed by the government representatives Liu and Geng, as well as the vote counters Qian and Pan.

▲ Important Resolutions

Next, the discussion focused on opposing the proposed 25% increase in water rates by the Shanghai Waterworks Company. After the chairman's report and a letter from the Shanghai Real Estate Association were presented, Yu Qiaqing, Chu Huiseng, Zhao Jinqing, Lin Kanghou, Lu Feibohong, Li Bohan, Pan Xulun, Yan Esheng, Xu Jiliao, and others spoke successively, discussing methods of opposition. He Deqiu explained that the Municipal Council and the Waterworks Company had entered into a contract on March 17, 1928, Article 13 of which stated that the Shanghai Waterworks Company could not change the water rates again within two years from July 1, 1929. An appendix to the article stated that after this period, if the Waterworks Company wished to increase rates, it had to submit the new budget to the Municipal Council for approval five months in advance. If the Municipal Council did not agree, each party could appoint a representative two months in advance to conduct arbitration. If the arbitrators could not resolve the matter, the British Consul-General or a representative designated by the British Consul-General would make the final decision. Therefore, the Waterworks Company's proposed rate increase and the Municipal Council's hasty approval were both in violation of this contract and disregarded the public opinion of the citizens. The following resolutions were passed unanimously: 1. A letter will be sent to the Municipal Council, stating that the proposed water rate increase is considered an increase in the burden on residents and a violation of the contract signed by the Municipal Council and the Waterworks Company in 1928, and that a serious reconsideration is necessary and the implementation should be stopped. 2. A letter will be sent to the Chinese Councilors, requesting them to unanimously advocate against the increase. 3. A letter will be sent to the Real Estate Association, requesting them to publish a notice to all property owners not to enter into new contracts with the Waterworks Company. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM. The texts of the various letters are recorded below:

▲ Director Bei's Letter of Resignation

To the Shanghai Concession Chinese Ratepayers' Association: I am writing to inform you that I will be traveling to the United States on business and will be leaving Shanghai soon. My itinerary will involve research and my stay will inevitably be lengthy, at least six months or more. The return date cannot be determined. Regarding the position of Chinese Director of the Municipal Council to which I was elected by your association, I believe that increasing the number of directors to five was achieved with great effort and through the combined efforts of the Chinese side. Since success was so hard-won, I should not be absent for a long period of time, lest it be criticized by foreigners. To demonstrate the seriousness of the Chinese in external affairs, I would like to request your association to elect another capable person to fill this position to facilitate progress. I humbly request that a meeting be convened as soon as possible to consider and implement this matter. I am deeply grateful. Sincerely, Bei Zuyi.

▲ Letter of Commendation to Director Bei

To Director Bei: Your letter of August 23rd has been received, stating that you will be traveling to the United States on business for more than six months and intend to resign from the position of Director of the Municipal Council. Our association considers this matter to be of great importance, and the Standing Committee and Executive Committee both believe that they have no power to decide. Therefore, a general meeting of representatives was convened today to discuss the matter. Everyone believed that you had to leave the country for several months to develop your bank's business. Although the public intention was to retain you, we had no choice but to reluctantly comply with your request. We believe that you have served the public and made many contributions, so you should be commended and thanked. We sincerely hope that you will return soon so that you can continue to serve the public. We are sending this letter to you with our best wishes for a pleasant journey.

▲ Notification to Director Hu

To Director Hu: It has been found that Mr. Bei Songsun, a director of our association attending the Municipal Council, will be leaving the country soon to go to Europe and America to study banking business and has submitted his resignation. After considering the facts, today's general meeting of representatives reluctantly complied with his request and held a vote to elect a replacement on the spot. As a result of the vote count, you were elected as the successor to the current term of the Municipal Council director. In addition to submitting a letter to the Municipal Council, we are sending this letter to inform you of this matter.

▲ Biography of Director Hu

Hu Zutong, courtesy name Mengjia, is a native of Yin County, Zhejiang Province. He is 43 years old and holds a Master's degree in Commerce from the University of Birmingham, England. He initially served as Deputy Manager of the Zhejiang Bank of Shanghai, then as Deputy Manager of the Bank of Communications of Shanghai, and was subsequently promoted to Manager. In the 17th year of the Republic (1928), the bank was reorganized and he was elected as General Manager. He currently also serves as a Director of the Shanghai Municipal Bank and Chairman of the Shanghai Banking Association.

▲ Important Letter Appendix

The Shanghai Real Estate Association sent a letter to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association the day before yesterday, which stated: We are writing to inform you that the proposed 25% increase in water rates in the Public Concession, which is scheduled to take effect on September 1st, will have a significant and profound impact on the lives of millions of residents within the concession. All residents within the concession are unanimously opposed to it. We understand that your association has included the opposition to the water rate increase on the agenda of the general meeting of representatives on September 5th, which demonstrates that your association is able to understand the interests of the residents within the concession and fulfill its responsibility of representing the opinions of all residents within the concession. We are very grateful. Our association has a warm enthusiasm for supporting your association's words and actions, and we should even more closely follow the opposition to the water rate increase. We are hereby presenting our collective views for your consideration and selection, and we request that you actively negotiate to revoke the Waterworks Company's proposed rate increase. First, water is used to supply residents' drinking water, and living things live by water. If they get it, they live; if they don't get it, they die. People's use of water is even more important. Therefore, in all countries in the world, the drinking water of cities is mostly directly managed by municipal authorities, so that residents can enjoy the right to cheap drinking water. Second, even if it is run by businesses, the drinking water price must be approved by the municipal authorities. On the one hand, it is licensed as a monopoly, originally hoping that citizens can also enjoy the right to cheap drinking water. The Waterworks Company is not subject to the pressure of competitors. Second, the municipal authority of the Public Concession is, in fact, the Municipal Council, so the right to approve the price of water also lies with the Municipal Council. However, the Public Concession's Municipal Council is the Municipal Council of all citizens within the concession, not the Municipal Council of the Waterworks Company. This kind of argument cannot be denied by anyone. Therefore, regarding the Waterworks Company's request for a rate increase, the Municipal Council, on the one hand, cannot deny the reasons for the Waterworks Company's request for a rate increase, and on the other hand, the interests of the millions of citizens within the concession who live by drinking water should also be given full consideration. Even if both interests cannot be taken together and both harms cannot be removed together, it seems that those that benefit the majority should be taken and those that harm the majority should be removed. The increase in water rates benefits a very small number of people and harms a very large number of people. Conversely, it benefits a very large number of people and harms a very small number of people. Third, the water price for Chinese-style houses was originally 5%. At that time, the rent for shops on the Great Horse Road was only 20 yuan per building. Later, the rent gradually increased, and the water price actually increased accordingly. Therefore, the water price collection rate did not change until the 16th year of the Republic (1927), when it was increased by 20%. In fact, the last rate increase was as unreasonable as this rate increase, because since the 11th year of the Republic (1922), Shanghai's rent has continued to increase due to supply and demand relations and price influences. Other various goods and services cannot be exceptions. However, since the price of water is calculated according to the rent, the conclusion is that the price rises with the rent. To put it clearly, if the rent rises by 30%, the water price will rise by 30%. In fact, the Waterworks Company has already been continuously increasing prices. Fourth, the Waterworks Company's biggest reason for requesting the Municipal Council to approve the rate increase is the decline in silver prices and the high cost of goods and labor. Regardless of the fact that it did not implement a price reduction when the London silver bar was at 61 pence in the first half of 1920, and taking a step back, the largest expenditure of other enterprises is raw materials, and the company does not have to pay for the water from the Huangpu River. In addition, there are no other public utilities that can obtain such free raw materials. If it is said that the price of water pipes has increased, it is necessary to increase the price to compensate. However, the Waterworks Company only installs large pipes, and the water pipes from the large pipes to the houses are all borne by the owners and paid to the company according to the price, and an additional installation fee is charged. Therefore, the impact of the decline in silver prices can be said to be very small. Sixth, other businesses have bad debts. For example, electricity, telephone, and even the Municipal Council's donations and taxes cannot be collected in full. However, the Waterworks Company does not have the risk of bad debts and has an unexpected benefit. For example, if the house has been rented out but is still being renovated, the water consumption is naturally not much, but the Waterworks Company can get more profit. Also, if the rent is 100 taels, including 6 taels for water, the actual rent is only 94 taels, but the Waterworks Company still calculates it according to 100 taels. Therefore, 3.67 cents are collected more for every 100 taels of rent. If there are rent arrears, the water bill is borne by the owner, so there will not be less money, and it is collected by the owner, so there is no cost to collect the money. This kind of business stability is not easy for people to seek and not easy to have. Sixth, the Waterworks Company has repeatedly said that the budget is not enough and the water bill must be increased. However, profit and loss are unavoidable for any enterprise. Since it has greatly benefited from the rise in silver prices, it is reasonable to accept the slight loss due to the fall in silver prices. Moreover, this is not the fault of the citizens who use drinking water, but a natural disaster that is similar to irresistible forces. Moreover, before the accounts of previous years are publicly audited, how can we not see the abuses of raising capital and arbitrarily spending money? Although we cannot judge the heart of a gentleman with the mind of a villain, this kind of possible thing is felt by the residents. Based on the above reasons, we dare to ask your association to allow our association to make the following requests: 1. Send a letter to the Municipal Council, immediately re-discuss the case, revoke the previous resolution approving the Waterworks Company's rate increase of 25%, and organize a committee to audit the company's accounts of previous years. If it must be implemented, the case concerns the interests of millions of residents and should be decided by a meeting of taxpayers to show special seriousness. 2. Send a letter to the attending Municipal Councilors, requesting that the case be reviewed at the Municipal Council's board of directors to achieve the goal of revoking the last resolution. The matter concerns the interests of millions of citizens within the concession. We do not mind spending time and effort to send this letter. We hope that you will handle it accordingly. We are very grateful. September 4, 1929.

Russian Tea Merchant Arrested and Released on Bail in Hankou 129

▲ Foreign Affairs Office Notifies Tea Association Representatives

A Russian named Rickman has been traveling between Shanghai and Hankou for many years, engaging in Chinese tea trade with Chinese merchants. Recently, he was arrested by the authorities for going to Hankou to purchase Chinese tea. The Shanghai Tea Association, believing that Rickman was a legitimate merchant, telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, requesting the Wuhan Headquarters to release him. Shipping Merchants Continue

Opposing Increased Fees for Night Work Permits 130

▲ Requesting Shipping Association to Ask Customs to Waive Increase

Shanghai is a major port for trade, with many commercial vessels coming and going every day. Each

Page 14

ship, due to limited schedules and large cargo volumes, may experience import delays or be required to export within a set timeframe, necessitating night work for loading. According to regulations, a "Night Work Permit" must be obtained from customs before night work can commence. The original fee for this permit was 10 taels per vessel per occasion. The Jianghai Customs suddenly announced an increase in fees, requiring an additional 80% of the original amount. Shanghai shipping merchants were shocked upon hearing this and jointly petitioned for a waiver. The Customs had already rejected the request. Yesterday, Shanghai shipping merchants submitted a second public petition in opposition, determined not to stop until the cancellation goal is achieved. Details of this matter are as follows:

▲ Customs Insists on Increasing Fees

The Jianghai Customs' increase in the Night Work Permit fee originally set at 10 taels per occasion, now wants to raise it to 18 taels. The Shanghai shipping merchants held a general meeting, believing that they cannot bear any further burden during this time of shipping industry decline. The Shipping Association sent a letter to the Chief Inspector of Customs requesting a waiver. The Chief Inspector of Customs replied, stating that the Night Work Permit fee was set 60 years ago. Due to rising prices, it is necessary to increase it. He also stated that it is up to the shipping merchants to buy or not, indicating that he is determined to implement it. The shipping companies have no room for interference or opposition.

▲ Shipping Merchants Oppose a Second Time

Upon receiving the Chief Inspector of Customs' reply, the Shanghai shipping merchants convened a general meeting. They decided to make another statement regarding the content of the reply, and still, in the name of all shipping merchants, sent a letter to the Shipping Association, requesting them to forward it to the Commissioner of Customs, urging them to cancel the fee increase. The original letter stated briefly: "We received the letter and learned that the Customs Commissioner's refusal to accept the request of the shipping merchants to withdraw the increase in the Night Work Permit fee is deeply disconcerting. After carefully examining the Chief Inspector of Customs' reply, the reasons for not being able to waive the increase are nothing more than that the Night Work Permit fee was set 60 years ago, and now prices are rising and expenses are huge, so it must be increased proportionally. It is also said that it is up to the shipping merchants to buy or not. We believe that the principle of the state establishing customs is to facilitate commercial transport. Merchants fulfill their obligation to pay taxes, and the state fulfills its responsibility to protect them. The regular expenses of customs are not intended to be compared to tax revenue. How can tax revenue be increased due to increased trivial expenses? If the customs fees are the standard for collecting taxes, then the various tax rules will inevitably be increased and changed at any time. Our shipping merchants invest huge amounts of capital, develop transportation for the country, and serve as a hub for the transportation of commercial goods. Their ship schedules are no less than the lifeblood of other merchants' goods. Any delay will result in the loss of that lifeblood. In order to seek speed and rush to do night work, applying for a Night Work Permit is nothing more than to avoid huge losses and facilitate commercial transport. Moreover, shipping vessels already bear extremely heavy taxes to customs, such as tonnage dues, ship inspection fees, and taxes on circulars and permits. There is also a tax on fumigation. In recent years, the overall situation has been unstable. In the event of war, Chinese vessels are requisitioned for military transport, suspension of navigation, and cessation of operations are common. The shipping industry is on the verge of bankruptcy. The state does not provide protection, but suddenly wants to increase the Night Work Permit fee by 80%. The customs' attitude towards our shipping merchants is close to harsh. (omitted below) We should request your association to send another letter to the Chief Customs Commissioner to strongly advocate that the increase in the Night Work Permit fee be waived in order to maintain the dying shipping industry." This letter can be sent out today.

Overseas Chinese Federation

Further Request to Rescind the Passport Law (Continued) 135

▲ Listing Ten Reasons

5. While issuing passports for both leaving and returning to the country might not entirely align with national circumstances, there are examples in other countries. However, requiring passport renewals during stays abroad is absolutely unnecessary. The Ministry of Interior's regulations for issuing certificates of nationality to overseas Chinese also stipulate that they are "for permanent retention and do not need to be exchanged." Article 11 of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Exit Passport Law states, "Passports are valid for one year. If continued residence is desired after expiration, the holder should present the old passport to the local or nearby Chinese embassy or consulate to exchange for a new one, paying the required fee. Failure to renew will render the old passport invalid." This forces overseas Chinese to pay eight yuan in passport fees every year, a disguised poll tax. It means that an overseas Chinese citizen residing abroad for a year and returning home for even a single day must obtain three passports, incurring a fee of twenty-four yuan. This is ten times shorter and less flexible than the temporary residence permits issued by the Dutch East Indies government, which are valid for two years and can be extended for another eight years free of charge. This confirms the statement made by Dutch envoy Oudendijk to Committee Member Qiu Xinyun that "the Dutch government's treatment of overseas Chinese is perhaps no worse than your own government." This could encourage the Dutch East Indies government to follow suit, forcing our overseas Chinese to renew their residence permits and pay fees annually. Other countries establish consulates to protect their overseas citizens, while our country establishes consulates to mistreat them. If the Ministry of Foreign Affairs were to reflect on this, they would surely be ashamed. This is the fifth reason why we must request a strict order to rescind this law to eliminate harsh practices and appease the expectations of overseas Chinese.

6. Article 9 of the Provisional Exit Passport Law states that applicants for exit passports must first fill out an application form, and those applying for ordinary passports must also submit a written request, along with the following guarantee documents, to the issuing agency for approval. Those leaving for business should provide a guarantee letter from two local chambers of commerce or reputable businesses, certifying their capital amount. Those leaving for work should provide a guarantee letter from two local labor unions or reputable businesses, certifying their work skills. This method might be feasible in Europe and America, but in our country, it's like using a mallet to carve a fine point. Does the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, with its deep and impenetrable doors, know that very few of our countrymen leaving the country do so with capital? They are either exploited by corrupt local bullies, suffer from the ravages of war or natural disasters, are driven out by communists, or are forced by bandits. Compelled to abandon their natural inclination to settle down, they sing a sorrowful song of leaving their homeland. On the day of departure, most are penniless, possessing nothing of value. Their families cannot predict their return, and most relatives and friends consider it a final farewell. Where would such poor people find guarantors? A small shop might be possible, but where to find a reputable business? One is difficult, let alone two. By demanding what is impossible for the poor, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is opening the door to extortion by travel agencies and issuing authorities. It forces those unable to cope with extortion to suffer the oppression of human and natural disasters, unable to escape the country even until death. It forces those unwilling to sit and wait for death to become communists and bandits. It is a prelude to restrictions on Chinese immigration by the Dutch, British, Japanese, American, French, Siamese, Portuguese, and other countries and colonies. We are discriminating against ourselves before others do. While others are advocating "southward expansion," the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is vigorously pursuing "southward retreat." While others are encouraging emigration, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is hindering it. While others are providing relief to the unemployed, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is creating unemployment. Does the Ministry of Foreign Affairs harbor some deep-seated animosity towards our people? The Premier is protecting overseas Chinese, while the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is mistreating them. The Premier is supporting farmers and laborers, while the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is destroying them. The Premier is promoting the people's livelihood, while the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is hindering it. Is the Ministry of Foreign Affairs betraying the Premier? This is the sixth reason why we must request a strict order to rescind this law to open up avenues for survival and rescue disaster victims.

7. Article 2 of the Provisional Return Passport Law states, "Applicants for return passports must present their exit passports to be issued. This does not apply to overseas Chinese children born abroad and naturalized citizens." At first glance, it seems comprehensive, but upon closer examination, it is actually difficult to implement. Some overseas Chinese left the country decades ago, are neither overseas students nor naturalized citizens, and left the country long before the current stringent passport laws were issued by foreign and warlord governments. At that time there was no need to apply for a passport, and of course no passport to present. Now that it is stipulated that new passports will not be issued without presenting old passports, and those without new passports will be investigated, it means that elderly emigrants who left the country before the promulgation of this passport law will never be able to re-enter the country. This is the seventh reason why we must request a strict order to rescind this law to correct errors and facilitate implementation.

8. According to a 1926 survey by the Straits Settlements government, a total of 348,593 overseas Chinese traveled from Xiamen, Hong Kong, Shantou, Haikou, and Guangzhou to Singapore. The number of those traveling directly from various locations to Annam, Siam, Burma, India, Penang, Malacca, the Federated Malay States, the Unfederated Malay States, the Dutch East Indies, the American Philippines, Japan, Korea, Taiwan, and the various continents of Europe, America, Africa, and Australia should be at least roughly equal to the number of those traveling to Singapore. This means that the number of people leaving our country each year is about 700,000. If calculated according to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' passport fee of eight yuan per passport, the annual revenue would be 5.6 million yuan. The number of people returning to the country is about two-thirds of the number of people leaving, generating another 3.7 million yuan. Adding the more than 11 million overseas Chinese residing abroad, if each person has to renew their passport annually and pay a fee of eight yuan, then there would be about 90 million yuan. Even if the actual revenue is not as high, the income is still significant. However, they are using their authority to illegally collect fees. We only hear that the consul in a certain port earns a certain amount of guilders in passport fees per term, and the consulate in a certain port earns a certain amount of yuan in passport fees per month, but the use of these funds is unclear. Although the Ministry of Foreign Affairs stipulates that funds be remitted to the ministry every three months, there is no public announcement of the actual revenue and expenditures. This is the eighth reason why we must request a strict order to rescind this law to unify finances and clarify governance.

9. Our country's nationality law follows the principle of jus sanguinis (right of blood), while the Dutch colonial nationality law follows the principle of jus soli (right of soil). Overseas Chinese born in Dutch colonies are considered Chinese citizens by our country, but are considered Dutch citizens by the Dutch. However, since reason cannot be completely extinguished and facts are difficult to change immediately, the Dutch government has never made a clear distinction between locally born and overseas Chinese students. In the past, overseas Chinese students participated in the Chinese Chamber of Commerce and held the Chinese Association without Dutch government interference. However, the Chinese Consul-General in Java, Zhang, in order to facilitate the collection of passport fees and avoid diplomatic disputes with the Dutch, openly acknowledged that overseas Chinese students returning to China must first obtain a Dutch passport and then have it signed by the Chinese consul. This completely treats overseas Chinese students as foreigners. If overseas Chinese students want to return to China, they must swallow their pride and become Dutch citizens, shamelessly obtaining a Dutch passport. Otherwise, the Chinese consul will not dare to issue a passport, and they will be detained without a passport. The mental anguish is extreme. In terms of foreign affairs, this means surrendering sovereignty and humiliating the country. In terms of overseas Chinese students, it means betrayal and self-destruction. This is not only heartbreaking for hundreds of thousands of overseas Chinese students, but also ridiculed by people all over the world. This is the ninth reason why we must request a strict order to rescind this law to restore national sovereignty and wash away national shame.

10. Before the promulgation of the Provisional Passport Law, the Dutch East Indies and the American Philippines had already implemented "overseas Chinese registration," with a registration fee of two Dutch guilders or two Philippine pesos, which had to be renewed annually. After the promulgation of the Provisional Passport Law, it is unclear whether the "overseas Chinese registration" item has been cancelled. If the two items are carried out in parallel, the overseas Chinese will be unable to bear the burden. This is the tenth reason why we must request a strict order to rescind this law to exempt repeated fees and show compassion for poor overseas Chinese. Based on these reasons, we urge your approval. If granted, all overseas Chinese will be grateful. After rescission, be able to recognize the particularly difficult situation of overseas Chinese migrating south, find ways to exempt passports, and restore the original state as before, which would be what overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia sincerely pray for. Otherwise, we earnestly request that you adopt the requests made in the Association's respectful telegram, stipulating that the passport fee for leaving and returning to the country be two dimes, and the stamp duty be two cents each, with full exemption for the poor. All the harsh practices of annual passport renewal, fee payment, replacement for loss or damage, and fee payment should be abolished. And the items in Article 11 of the Exit Passport Law concerning the guarantee of capital amount and work skills by reputable businesses, and the guarantee by legal institutions that tourists will not engage in any business after leaving the country should be deleted. Then the so-called passport will be worthy of its name. We earnestly submit our plea, feeling uneasy as we await your order. Respectfully, the Overseas Chinese Federation. (End)

Local News Two

Jiang Baozhen Escapes Kidnapping in the Rain, Rescued Half an Hour After Abduction 136

▲ Police Obtain Information and Capture Bandit Vehicle

▲ Car Overturns into Ditch, Hostage Survives

On the 28th of last month, Zhou Rangsan, a Chinese employee of Mobil Oil, was kidnapped by bandits at the entrance of his alley residence on Hardoon Road. After the incident, the victim reported it to the Jing'an Temple Police Station, who immediately dispatched Chinese and Western detectives in vehicles to search for the perpetrators. They encountered the bandit vehicle on Hongqiao Road, arrested one bandit, and extracted the location of the hostage, rescuing Zhou. The entire ordeal, from abduction to escape, lasted only three hours, a feat praised by the police force. Yesterday, another Ningbo native, Jiang Baozhen, was abducted by bandits on Xinza Gate Bridge Road around 9:30 AM. After the victim's chauffeur reported it to the Jing'an Temple Police Station, the police followed the same procedure, dispatching armed detectives in cars to patrol the roads in the western district. They eventually spotted the car carrying the hostage near the intersection of Hongqiao Road and Haig Road and gave chase. The bandits, panicked, overturned the car into a ditch and abandoned the hostage, fleeing the scene. Jiang was able to escape from the bandits' clutches, approximately half an hour after being abducted, amidst heavy rain.

▲ The kidnapped Ningbo native, Jiang Baozhen, is 53 years old and made his fortune in the construction industry. He resides at 445 Xinza Gate Bridge Road and owns a Buick car for transportation, with license plate number 10051. His chauffeur, Ah Mao, was hired last year. Yesterday morning, at 9:30 AM, Ah Mao had just finished cleaning and parking the car outside the gate, waiting for his employer to use it. Unbeknownst to him, three bandits were lying in wait by the roadside. Upon seeing Jiang enter the car, one bandit drew a gun and ordered chauffeur Ah Mao not to make a sound, jumping into the passenger seat to monitor his actions. The remaining bandits entered the back of the car, flanking Jiang Baozhen on both sides, and ordered the chauffeur to drive off. Jiang had originally intended to go to his office on Fujian Road, but now he was at the mercy of the bandits, unable to escape.

▲ Escape After abducting the "God of Wealth," the bandits forced the chauffeur to drive west. At the intersection of Hardoon Road, the car stopped temporarily, and the chauffeur, Ah Mao, was driven out. Then, the bandits drove off themselves, leaving a trail of dust. Ah Mao immediately rushed to the Jing'an Temple Road Police Station to report the kidnapping of his employer and the hijacking of car number 10051. Upon receiving the information, Chinese and Western detectives from the police station immediately armed themselves and drove off in cars to search for the stolen vehicle in the western district, including Daxi Road and Hongqiao Road. Near the intersection of Hongqiao Road and Haig Road, they spotted a car driving straight ahead, with license plate number 10051. The police car accelerated and gave chase. Hearing someone pursuing them from behind, the bandits drove frantically. Unfortunately, it was raining heavily, the road was very slippery, and the road was extremely narrow. In a moment of panic, the bandits' car tires slipped into a ditch by the roadside, rendering the car immobile. They abandoned the hostage and fled for their lives. Jiang Baozhen was helped out of the car by the detectives. Although he was fortunate to be unharmed, he was also in a state of shock. He glanced at his watch, which read ten o'clock, and the sky cleared up, with sunlight shining over the fields. Jiang, upon returning home, expressed his gratitude for his narrow escape.

Abducted a Large Number of Crew Members 138

Recently, bandits have gathered off the coast of Wusongkou in the Juegang sea area, and the fishermen in that area have fled.
